4388<div>

4389<h2>

4390All-Weather Durability&mdash;Outdoor Furniture Must-Haves</h2>

4391

4392</div>

4393</div>

4394</div>

4395</div>

4396<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-TEXTBLOCK-d--b--ba">

4397<div>

4398<div class=" TextBlock-module_textBlockContainer__X2cPA">

4399<div>

4400<p>

4401Whether you&rsquo;re looking to lounge comfortably on your back deck or host your neighborhood barbeque, choosing durable furniture materials that stand up to the weather is a must. Here are all the qualities you should look for before you purchase any <a href="https://vevano.com/catalog/furniture-outdoor/">

4402outdoor furniture set</a>

4403.</p>

4404

4405

4406<h3>

4407Water Resistance&mdash;Prevents Stains, Rust, and Mold</h3>

4408

4409

4410<p>

4411It&rsquo;d be a waste to put furniture outside just for it to quickly be damaged by rain, humidity, and other moisture. That&rsquo;s why water resistance is a must-have feature for any outdoor furniture!</p>

4412

4413

4414<p>

4415Many outdoor furniture materials are used specifically for their ability to withstand moisture and prevent warping, watermarks, or rotting. If you&rsquo;re in the market for new outdoor fabric, keep in mind that water resistance is a major factor in stain resistance. Thankfully, if the material you choose is not naturally water resistant, you can get water-resistant covers.</p>

4416

4417

4418<p>

4419A secondary concern with the moisture that could accumulate on your furniture is mold and mildew. However, some materials (like polyester) aren&#39;t water resistant but are either chemically treated or&nbsp;naturally resist mold and mildew. Especially in extremely humid climates, it&rsquo;s important to check that the material you choose for your outdoor couches or chairs is chemically treated to resist mold and mildew.</p>

4420

4421

4422<p>

4423Lastly, no one wants rusty furniture, so make sure if you choose metal furniture pieces look for anti-rust features so it stays beautiful no matter how much moisture builds up.</p>

4424

4425

4426<h3>

4427UV Resistance&mdash;Prevents Colors from Fading</h3>

4428

4429

4430<p>

4431Even with covered patios or decks, quite a bit of sunlight will hit your outdoor furniture every day. UV or fade resistant materials won&rsquo;t be bleached easily by the sun, so your furniture will stay as vibrant as the day you brought them home for a significant amount of time.</p>

4432

4433

4434<h3>

4435Weight&mdash;Determines Wind Resistance &amp; Ease of Arrangement</h3>

4436

4437

4438<p>

4439Especially in windy locations, heavy furniture is great for keeping things from flying away. But if it&rsquo;s too heavy, rearranging your furniture can be nearly impossible. Make sure to buy something in the middle&mdash;heavy enough to stay on the ground by light enough you can move it.</p>

4440

4441

4442<h3>

4443Temperature Resistance&mdash;Keeps Your Furniture Comfortable &amp; Stable</h3>

4444

4445

4446<p>

4447Your outdoor furniture is going to experience all kinds of weather changes, so you want to find materials that are resistant to changes due to temperature. Metal is great at maintaining shape in both hot and cool weather, while wood and some plastics can swell or crack with changing temperatures.</p>

4448

4449

4450<p>

4451Also, look for options that don&rsquo;t get hot. Consider buying lighter colored materials and use umbrellas or other sun-shields to prevent your furniture from getting hot enough to burn your skin.</p>

4452

4453

4454<h3>

4455Easy to Clean&mdash;Helps Furniture Last Longer &amp; Look Better</h3>

4456

4457

4458<p>

4459Windblown debris like dirt and dust will accumulate easily on the surfaces of your outdoor furniture, so it&rsquo;s important to choose materials that are easy to clean and maintain. Additionally, it helps to find furniture with earthy colors or patterns that can disguise any dirt or other blemishes between each clean. Our guide to <a href="https://vevano.com/resource-center/how-to-clean-outdoor-cushions/">

4460cleaning outdoor cushions </a>

4461and other outdoor furniture can give you an idea of how to maintain patio furniture, especially fabrics.</p>

4462

4463</div>

4464</div>

4465</div>

4466</div>

4467</div>

4468</div>

4469</div>

4470</div>

4471</div>

4472</div>

4473</div>

4474</div>

4475</div>

4499<img class="dafbf--b-fd-dece-image" src="https://img.vevano.com/fGqnDx8CDArSYPVp3JGipNS-oqficFey2i1MOdkTzuE/rs:fill:0:0/q:80/aHR0cHM6Ly9jZG4udmV2YW5vLmNvbS9CbG9nL3Jlc291cmNlLWNlbnRlci9iZXN0LW1hdGVyaWFscy1vdXRkb29yLWZ1cm5pdHVyZS9tZXRhbC1vdXRkb29yLWZ1cm5pdHVyZS1jaGFydC5wbmc" alt="Metal outdoor furniture comparison chart" title="Metal outdoor furniture comparison chart"/>

4507<p>

4508Metal is one of the most durable and versatile materials you can use in outdoor furniture. Because it&rsquo;s extremely malleable, it can be formed into a great variety of shapes and styles to match any aesthetic. Most metal furniture is combined with other furniture materials&mdash;like fabric cushions and backrests&mdash;to add comfort.</p>

4509

4510

4511<p>

4512Lots of manufactures have found techniques to produce metal furniture without the need for bolts or screws, reducing how likely it is to break and need repair or replacement. Some metals can get really hot in the sun, so it&rsquo;s important to consider that before you make your purchases. Let&rsquo;s look closer at the unique characteristics of each type of metal furniture.</p>

4746Steel is an extremely strong, durable metal that is great for heavier furniture pieces like tables and sofas. It&rsquo;s resistant to damage from extreme temperatures (though it still gets hot to the touch) and is resistant to rust and corrosion. Steel offers a sleek modern style that can add class to our outdoor spaces. Here are the top pros and cons you should consider with steel.</p>

4790 Resists Wind</strong>

4791&mdash;Many homeowners choose steel because it&rsquo;s too heavy to be blown over in windy conditions, but it&rsquo;s still light enough to be moved easily.</p>

4793

4794<p>

4795<strong>

4796 Eco-friendly</strong>

4797&mdash;Steel is often made with recycled material.</p>

4927<p>

4928Wrought iron is popular for outdoor furniture because it&rsquo;s highly&nbsp;workable and is often handcrafted into a variety of intricate designs. Wrought iron is the strongest metal used in outdoor furniture, but it&rsquo;s often&nbsp; heavy and requires more maintenance to keep it rust-free.</p>

4971 Durable</strong>

4972&mdash;Wrought iron is strong and won&rsquo;t buckle under weight. With proper care it can last up to 100 years.&nbsp;However, because of its vulnerability to rust, we do give iron a 2 out of 3 for durability when considering all-weather conditions.</p>

4975<p>

4976<strong>

4977 Resists Wind</strong>

4978&mdash;Wrought iron is perfect for windy areas because it&rsquo;s so heavy. However, that can also make it very difficult to move.</p>

5042<p>

5044 High Maintenance</strong>

Some newer varieties of wrought iron are treated with weather-resistant finishes to mitigate rust. Letting dirt accumulate on your chairs or tables can make it difficult to remove later.</p>

5048<p>

5050 Uncomfortable</strong>

5051&mdash;Because wrought iron is so rigid and uncomfortable, many furniture sets will also include fabric seats and backrests. Wrought iron also absorbs the same temperature of its environment, making your furniture hot in the summer and cold in the winter.</p>

5222<div>

5223<h2>

5224Best Wood Patio Materials: Teak &amp; Eucalyptus</h2>

5225

5226</div>

5227</div>

5228</div>

5229</div>

5230<div class="Layout-module_hidden-xs__2UQIp Layout-module_visible-sm__Z2eD8 Layout-module_visible-md__1t5sZ Layout-module_visible-lg__1PfV6 visibility-plugin-wrapper">

5231<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-SINGLE_IMAGE-ba--f--ddcc">

5232<div class="SingleImage-module_singleImage__3fWXf ba--f--ddcc-singleImageAlignment">

5233<img class="ba--f--ddcc-image" src="https://img.vevano.com/rxRMzmaIsqqO64NfaN7Jidwhh1UsdUrp4LQ7LN_Uzz4/rs:fill:0:0/q:80/aHR0cHM6Ly9jZG4udmV2YW5vLmNvbS9CbG9nL3Jlc291cmNlLWNlbnRlci9iZXN0LW1hdGVyaWFscy1vdXRkb29yLWZ1cm5pdHVyZS93b29kLW91dGRvb3ItZnVybml0dXJlLWNoYXJ0LnBuZw" alt="best outdoor wood furniture materials comparison chart" title="best outdoor wood furniture materials comparison chart"/>

5234</div>

5238<div>

5239<div class=" TextBlock-module_textBlockContainer__X2cPA">

5240<div>

5241<p>

5242While you can find outdoor furniture made from almost any wood, by far the most popular are Teak and Eucalyptus. Teak is sourced from Asian countries like Burma and Thailand while Eucalyptus comes from Australia and surrounding islands. One important thing to always look for with any wood furniture is its FSC rating&mdash;the degree to which it uses recycled wood or is harvested from sustainable sources.</p>

5243

5244

5245<p>

5246Though they come from different regions of the world, these two woods have similar style, strength, weather resistance, and maintenance needs. Both varieties need to be oiled or stained about once a year to maintain their original colors and prevent other damage.</p>

5309<div>

5310<p>

5311Teak outdoor furniture offers a unique modern and minimalist style to your deck or patio. The great thing about using teak instead of other woods is it&rsquo;s natural resistance to weather conditions because it has a high resin content. Let&rsquo;s take a closer look at some pros and cons.</p>

5339<div>

5340<h4>

5341<span style="color:#696969;">

5342<span style="font-size:20px;">

5343Pros</span>

5344</span>

5345</h4>

5346

5347

5348<p>

5349<strong>

5350 Durable</strong>

5351&mdash;Teak is an extremely durable, dense wood that makes it great for outdoor use. It naturally resists pests and generally doesn&rsquo;t rot easily. Like any wood it will crack and swell with use, but that doesn&rsquo;t generally affect the integrity of your furniture.</p>

5352

5353

5354<p>

5355<strong>

5356 Strong</strong>

5357&mdash;The dense nature of teak plus its binding resins make it super strong. It&rsquo;s great for making both chairs and tables.</p>

5358

5359

5360<p>

5361<strong>

5362 Temperature Resistant</strong>

5363&mdash;Don&rsquo;t worry about your teak furniture getting too hot or two cold! This wood naturally moderates heat in all seasons.</p>

5364

5365

5366<h4>

5367&nbsp;</h4>

5368

5369

5370<ul>

5371

5372</ul>

5373

5374</div>

5375</div>

5376</div>

5377</div>

5378</div>

5379</div>

5380</div>

5381</div>

5382<div class="Layout-module_omnimerse-column-sm-6__2LJO_ Layout-module_marginTopOnSmall__2rO47 merce-column">

5383<div class="">

5384<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-COLUMN-fefda-d-ba--bcb">

5385<div class="merce-column-container">

5386<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-TEXTBLOCK-afc-f-b-bf-bcfbc">

5387<div>

5388<div class=" TextBlock-module_textBlockContainer__X2cPA">

5389<div>

5390<h4>

5391<span style="font-size:20px;">

5392Cons</span>

5393</h4>

5394

5395

5396<p>

5397<strong>

5398 Color Fades</strong>

5399&mdash;Under the sun and weather changes, the natural color of teak fades to a silvery-grey hue. It&rsquo;s not a complete con because the color is beautiful and a natural part of teak&rsquo;s aging process, but if you prefer the original color of the wood it requires more care like oiling and staining your furniture regularly.</p>

5400

5401

5402<p>

5403<strong>

5404 Not Always Eco-friendly</strong>

5405&mdash;Over the years, the rise in popularity of teak has increased the amount of clear-cutting happening in Asian forests. It&rsquo;s difficult to find teak furniture that has been sustainably sourced. Recently, however, companies like Reforest Teak have started reforestation efforts to sustainably source all their teak furniture.</p>

5406

5407

5408<p>

5409<strong>

5410 Price</strong>

5411&mdash;The popularity and environmental factors play right into the price of teak. Because demand is up and the material is becoming more scarce as deforestation continues, teak is one of the most expensive options for outdoor furniture.</p>

5422<span style="color:#696969;">

5423<span style="font-size:20px;">

5424Care Tips</span>

5425</span>

5426</h4>

5427

5428

5429<ul>

5430

5431 <li>

5432Address spills immediately by wiping with a soft, dry cloth</li>

5433

5434 <li>

5435Clean with warm soapy water, then dry with a soft, clean cloth</li>

5436

5437 <li>

5438Avoid the use of harsh cleaners and abrasives</li>

5439

5440 <li>

5441Avoid letting water stand on the surface of all teak furniture</li>

5442

5443 <li>

5444Cover when not in use</li>

5445

5446 <li>

5447If the finish starts to peel away, gently remove with a soft bristle brush</li>

5448

5449</ul>

5617<h3>

5618Eucalyptus</h3>

5619

5620</div>

5621</div>

5622</div>

5623</div>

5624<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-SINGLE_IMAGE-dcfedff-bdb-c-c-edeeac">

5626<img class="dcfedff-bdb-c-c-edeeac-image" src="https://img.vevano.com/3TOXG0Acw6w-J1cvnLmjKMDPyqP6ovl3yXW95dp_uEg/rs:fill:0:0/q:80/aHR0cHM6Ly9jZG4udmV2YW5vLmNvbS9CbG9nL3Jlc291cmNlLWNlbnRlci9iZXN0LW1hdGVyaWFscy1vdXRkb29yLWZ1cm5pdHVyZS9ldWNhbHlwdHVzLW91dGRvb3ItZnVybml0dXJlLW1hdGVyaWFscy5qcGc" alt="Outdoor furniture chair made of wood" title="Outdoor furniture chair made of wood"/>

5650<div>

5651<p>

5652If you want a similar style and look to teak but don&rsquo;t want the price tag or the environmental impact, eucalyptus is the way to go! It has nearly all the same benefits of teak but costs less and is more environmentally-friendly.</p>

5679<div>

5680<h4>

5681<span style="color:#696969;">

5682<span style="font-size:20px;">

5683Pros</span>

5684</span>

5685</h4>

5686

5687

5688<p>

5689<strong>

5690 Durable</strong>

5691&mdash;Eucalyptus is just as dense as teak and has&nbsp;a similar resin content that helps keep pests away and the wood rot resistant. It will swell and crack with use, but remains strong. However, compared to teak, eucalyptus is slightly less durable which is which is why it gets a 2 out of 3 for durability from us.</p>

5692

5693

5694<p>

5695<strong>

5696 Environmentally Friendly</strong>

5697&mdash;One of the biggest advantages that eucalyptus has over teak is that it&rsquo;s more sustainable. There is a larger supply (nearly 75% of the forest in Australia has eucalyptus) and it grows quickly, so most suppliers harvest from replanted growth instead of cutting down established forests.</p>

5698

5699

5700<p>

5701<strong>

5702 Price</strong>

5703&mdash;Because of the increased supply and better environmental impact, eucalyptus is much less expensive than teak.</p>

5732&mdash;Just like teak, eucalyptus will fade to a silvery-grey hue if not sanded, oiled, and stained regularly.</p>

5733

5734

5735<p>

5736<strong>

5737 Not Ideal for Cold Climates</strong>

5738&mdash;Eucalyptus may splinter and crack in cold temperatures. Be sure to store any Eucalyptus furniture items during the winter.</p>

5832<h2>

5833Plastic &amp; Synthetic Resin Patio Furniture Materials</h2>

5834

5835</div>

5836</div>

5837</div>

5838</div>

5839<div class="Layout-module_hidden-xs__2UQIp Layout-module_visible-sm__Z2eD8 Layout-module_visible-md__1t5sZ Layout-module_visible-lg__1PfV6 visibility-plugin-wrapper">

5840<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-SINGLE_IMAGE-cbddd-ec-e--ebbbb">

5841<div class="SingleImage-module_singleImage__3fWXf cbddd-ec-e--ebbbb-singleImageAlignment">

5842<img class="cbddd-ec-e--ebbbb-image" src="https://img.vevano.com/YP-Fd6Y79p7GNNpSJkueyZKXMrzsnJnYzr_2ULOOmkY/rs:fill:0:0/q:80/aHR0cHM6Ly9jZG4udmV2YW5vLmNvbS9CbG9nL3Jlc291cmNlLWNlbnRlci9iZXN0LW1hdGVyaWFscy1vdXRkb29yLWZ1cm5pdHVyZS9wbGFzdGljLW91dGRvb3ItZnVybml0dXJlLWNoYXJ0LnBuZw" alt="plastic outdoor furniture comparison chart" title="plastic outdoor furniture comparison chart"/>

5843</div>

5844</div>

5845</div>

5846<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-TEXTBLOCK-dfecf--b-b-eddfacb">

5847<div>

5848<div class=" TextBlock-module_textBlockContainer__X2cPA">

5849<div>

5850<p>

5851Looking for something extremely durable, lightweight, and affordable? It&rsquo;s time for you to check out the world of plastic and resin furniture pieces. Plastic and resin choices are a popular replacement for the bamboo, rattan, and willow that has been traditionally used to make wicker furniture. (Note: Wicker is often confused as a material name, but it&rsquo;s actually the name of the weaving technique.) Let&rsquo;s take a deeper look at the different kinds of plastic furniture and the benefits they offer.</p>

5880Polyethylene Synthetic Resin</h3>

5914<div>

5915<p>

5916Polyethylene is a synthetic resin that is commonly used for wicker furniture because it can mimic plant fibers like rattan. The higher quality version of polyethylene is known as high density polyethylene or HDPE. This is one of the most popular plastics used in wicker outdoor furniture because it is lightweight, easy make into any style, and&nbsp;extremely durable.</p>

5944<h4>

5945<span style="color:#696969;">

5946<span style="font-size:20px;">

5947Pros</span>

5948</span>

5949</h4>

5950

5951

5952<p>

5953<strong>

5954 Fade Resistant</strong>

5955&mdash;With polyethylene, there&rsquo;s pretty much no worry that your sunbathing habits will fade your furniture! Some other plastics are painted which can chip or fade to unattractive colors under the surface. Instead of using paint, the color of polyethylene is embedded all the way through the plastic strands, so there&rsquo;s no worry about sun damage or paint chips.</p>

5956

5957

5958<p>

5959<strong>

5960 Resistant to All Weather Concerns</strong>

5961&mdash;Plastic furniture like polyethylene are resistant to water, mold and mildew, and other weather-related damage.</p>

5962

5963

5964<p>

5965<strong>

5966 Budget-Friendly</strong>

5967&mdash;The advantage of buying this synthetic material is that it&rsquo;s one of the most inexpensive outdoor furniture materials on the market.</p>

5989</span>

5990</h4>

5991

5992

5993<p>

5994<strong>

5995 Not as Eco-friendly as Natural Fiber</strong>

5996&mdash;As with any plastic or resin, polyethylene isn&rsquo;t as compostable&nbsp;as natural fibers or materials. However, HDPE is one of the more eco-friendly plastic and resin options available because it is made of 100% recycled material.</p>

6058<h3>

6059Polypropylene Synthetic Resin</h3>

6061</div>

6093<div>

6094<p>

6095Polypropylene&mdash;more commonly known as poly&mdash;is a form of thermoplastic polymer resin. It&rsquo;s derived from recycled plastic bottles, milk jugs, and other plastic containers, making it an environmentally-friendly choice for outdoor furniture. Because it&rsquo;s easy to manufacture and is highly durable, it has become the most popular material for outdoor furniture. Let&rsquo;s explore the pros and cons of poly!</p>

6123<h4>

6124<span style="color:#696969;">

6125<span style="font-size:20px;">

6126Pros</span>

6127</span>

6128</h4>

6129

6130

6131<p>

6132<strong>

6133 Fade Resistant</strong>

6134&mdash;Just like polyethylene, polypropylene is colored all the way through the plastic so it won&rsquo;t chip or fade.</p>

6135

6136

6137<p>

6138<strong>

6139 Resistant to All Weather Concerns</strong>

6140&mdash;Poly checks every box when it comes to weather-related outdoor furniture concerns. It&rsquo;s waterproof, mold and mildew resistant, fade resistant, and damage resistant. Poly is so strong it can&rsquo;t withstand a lot of force and pressure before it breaks.</p>

6141

6142

6143<p>

6144<strong>

6145 Lightweight</strong>

6146&mdash;If you think you&rsquo;ll rearrange your outdoor furniture frequently, poly is the way to go. Though more prone to toppling in the wind than steel or iron furniture, compared to PVC and other resin or plastic furniture options, poly is usually weighted enough to withstand heavy winds.</p>

6147

6148

6149<p>

6150<strong>

6151 Budget-Friendly</strong>

6152&mdash;This is one of the most inexpensive materials on the market!</p>

6277<p>

6278PVC is one of the most widely used plastics out there. It&rsquo;s really versatile&mdash;you&rsquo;ll find it used for plumping, packaging, toys, and more. It&rsquo;s even used in outdoor furniture, but unfortunately it&rsquo;s not always the best material to be used outside. Let&rsquo;s take a look at the pros and cons of this material.</p>

6509 Highly Flammable</strong>

6510&mdash;Summer is the time you want to use outdoor furniture the most, but with PVC you can run the risk of a fire if it gets too hot! Even if it doesn&rsquo;t go up in flames, extreme heat can cause PVC to release toxic fumes.</p>

6643<p>

6644Acrylic fabrics have long been a favorite for outdoor furniture, and Sunbrella is one of the best kinds! Sunbrella is one of the most versatile outdoor fabrics and comes in many colors and styles. Let&rsquo;s take a look at the pros and cons!</p>

6648

6649</ul>

6680Pros</span>

6683

6684

6685<p>

6686<strong>

6687 Fade-Resistant</strong>

6688&mdash;Sunbrella is one of the most fade resistant outdoor fabrics there is because it has UV resistant properties. This means that it will last longer than most other outdoor fabrics.</p>

6689

6690

6691<p>

6692<strong>

6693 Water and Mildew Resistant</strong>

6694&mdash;Fabric is more susceptible to water damage and mildew than other outdoor materials, which is why Sunbrella is so great! You don&rsquo;t have to worry much about water and mildew damage with Sunbrella cushions and pillows.</p>

6722 Comfort</strong>

6723&mdash;Sunbrella can be a bit scratchy, but usually doesn&rsquo;t bother people too much.</p>

6724

6725

6726<p>

6727<strong>

6728 Static Shocks&mdash;</strong>

6729Unlike olefin, Sunbrella&nbsp;transmits static electricity and may shock you!</p>

6730

6731

6732<p>

6733<strong>

6734 Cost</strong>

6735&mdash;Most acrylic outdoor fabrics like Sunbrella are expensive, but they last a long time.</p>

6895&mdash;Olefin is not quite as fade-resistant as Sunbrella, but it still has a significant lifespan under sunlight.</p>

6901&mdash;Even though olefin is a plastic, it often uses recycled plastics and process results in very little waste, making it environmentally-friendly.</p>

7019<div class="styles-plugin-outer custom-outer-style-ROW-baabe---f-bbddbedce">

7020<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-ROW-baabe---f-bbddbedce">

7021<div class="Row-module_global__1T17H merce-row-container">

7022<div class="Layout-module_row__3IzXF merce-row">

7023<div class="Layout-module_omnimerse-column-sm-12__29AUW Layout-module_marginTopOnSmall__2rO47 merce-column">

7024<div class="">

7025<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-COLUMN-bed-daa--a-dfd">

7026<div class="merce-column-container">

7027<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-TEXTBLOCK-edeb-d--ae-fddacb">

7028<div>

7029<div class=" TextBlock-module_textBlockContainer__X2cPA">

7030<div>

7031<p>

7032Polyester is a widely used fabric for anything from clothing to furniture&mdash;especially outdoor furniture. Polyester can be a good choice if you are looking for something that&rsquo;s resistant to moisture and weather but don&rsquo;t want to spend as much to get Sunbrella or olefin.</p>

7033

7034

7035<ul>

7036

7037</ul>

7038

7039</div>

7040</div>

7041</div>

7042</div>

7043</div>

7044</div>

7045</div>

7046</div>

7047</div>

7048</div>

7049</div>

7050</div>

7051</div>

7052<div class="">

7053<div class="styles-plugin-outer custom-outer-style-ROW-db-ab--c-fcecfa">

7054<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-ROW-db-ab--c-fcecfa">

7055<div class="Row-module_global__1T17H merce-row-container">

7056<div class="Layout-module_row__3IzXF merce-row">

7057<div class="Layout-module_omnimerse-column-sm-6__2LJO_ Layout-module_marginTopOnSmall__2rO47 merce-column">

7058<div class="">

7059<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-COLUMN-ddc-c--f-c">

7060<div class="merce-column-container">

7061<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-TEXTBLOCK-aaac-e-c-cc-fbae">

7062<div>

7063<div class=" TextBlock-module_textBlockContainer__X2cPA">

7064<div>

7065<h4>

7066<span style="color:#696969;">

7067<span style="font-size:20px;">

7068Pros</span>

7069</span>

7070</h4>

7071

7072

7073<p>

7074<strong>

7075 Quick-Drying (Though Not Waterproof)</strong>

7076&mdash;Outdoor furniture gets wet a lot, especially when used outside a backyard pool. Polyester is great because it&rsquo;s quick-drying to help you get back to using it without getting wet. However, polyester is still less water resistant than Sunbrella and olefin and may be more likely to stain.</p>

7077

7078

7079<p>

7080<strong>

7081 Budget-Friendly</strong>

7082&mdash;Polyester is the most budget-friendly outdoor fabric available.</p>

7083

7084</div>

7085</div>

7086</div>

7087</div>

7088</div>

7089</div>

7090</div>

7091</div>

7092<div class="Layout-module_omnimerse-column-sm-6__2LJO_ Layout-module_marginTopOnSmall__2rO47 merce-column">

7093<div class="">

7094<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-COLUMN-b--a-dc-bbccd">

7095<div class="merce-column-container">

7096<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-TEXTBLOCK-ad-d-cae-bd-dceeb">

7097<div>

7098<div class=" TextBlock-module_textBlockContainer__X2cPA">

7099<div>

7100<h4>

7101<span style="color:#696969;">

7102<span style="font-size:20px;">

7103Cons</span>

7104</span>

7105</h4>

7106

7107

7108<p>

7109<strong>

7110 Not Very Durable</strong>

7111&mdash;Polyester doesn&rsquo;t hold up as long as olefin or Sunbrella will. When looking at polyester outdoor furniture, you have to pay careful attention to the GSM number, which tells you how thick the fabric is. The higher the number, the thicker and more durable the fabric is.</p>

7112

7113

7114<ul>

7115

7116</ul>

7117

7118</div>

7119</div>

7120</div>

7121</div>

7122<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-TEXTBLOCK-fcbb-b-a-a-fbeaaacab">

7124<div class=" TextBlock-module_textBlockContainer__X2cPA">

7125<div>

7126<h4>

7127<span style="color:#696969;">

7128<span style="font-size:20px;">

7129Care Tips</span>

7130</span>

7131</h4>

7132

7133

7134<ul>

7135

7136 <li>

7137Wash with soap and water</li>

7138

7139 <li>

7140Allow to air dry</li>

7141

7142 <li>

7143Stain remover may used on stubborn stains</li>

7144

7145 <li>

7146Cover when not in use to reduce fading</li>

7147

7148</ul>

7199<h2>

7200Trending Outdoor Furniture: Concrete</h2>

7201

7202</div>

7256<div class=" TextBlock-module_textBlockContainer__X2cPA">

7257<div>

7258<p>

7259One last outdoor furniture material to talk about is concrete. Yes, the same material we use for sidewalks is used in outdoor furniture&mdash;often as tables rather than chairs or benches (though you will see it used for everything.) Concrete is usually a great statement piece when paired with wood or the bright colors of plastic furniture. Let&rsquo;s see what some of the pros and cons are of using concrete.</p>

7260

7261</div>

7262</div>

7263</div>

7264</div>

7265</div>

7266</div>

7267</div>

7268</div>

7269</div>

7270</div>

7271</div>

7272</div>

7273</div>

7274<div class="">

7275<div class="styles-plugin-outer custom-outer-style-ROW-e-d-fd-df-bde">

7276<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-ROW-e-d-fd-df-bde">

7277<div class="Row-module_global__1T17H merce-row-container">

7278<div class="Layout-module_row__3IzXF merce-row">

7279<div class="Layout-module_omnimerse-column-sm-6__2LJO_ Layout-module_marginTopOnSmall__2rO47 merce-column">

7280<div class="">

7281<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-COLUMN-aea-c--ec-efabd">

7282<div class="merce-column-container">

7283<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-TEXTBLOCK-eedcb-a-d--abace">

7284<div>

7285<div class=" TextBlock-module_textBlockContainer__X2cPA">

7286<div>

7287<h4>

7288<span style="color:#696969;">

7289<span style="font-size:20px;">

7290Pros</span>

7291</span>

7292</h4>

7293

7294

7295<p>

7296<strong>

7297 Durable</strong>

7298&mdash;Concrete is very hard and durable, so it will last long outside. It&rsquo;s extremely resistant to weather and will last for a long time.</p>

7299

7300

7301<p>

7302<strong>

7303 Price</strong>

7304&mdash;Concrete is going to be more expensive than plastic furniture, but might not cost quite as much as teak or eucalyptus.</p>

7305

7306</div>

7307</div>

7308</div>

7309</div>

7310</div>

7311</div>

7312</div>

7313</div>

7314<div class="Layout-module_omnimerse-column-sm-6__2LJO_ Layout-module_marginTopOnSmall__2rO47 merce-column">

7315<div class="">

7316<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-COLUMN-fe-d--b-abcfb">

7317<div class="merce-column-container">

7318<div class="styles-plugin-inner custom-inner-style-TEXTBLOCK-dbe-e-d-ae-bccfcf">

7319<div>

7320<div class=" TextBlock-module_textBlockContainer__X2cPA">

7321<div>

7322<h4>

7323<span style="color:#696969;">

7324<span style="font-size:20px;">

7325Cons</span>

7326</span>

7327</h4>

7328

7329

7330<p>

7331<strong>

7332 Comfort</strong>

7333&mdash;Concrete is the hardest outdoor furniture material you can find, which is why it&rsquo;s not usually used for chairs or couches. It works much better for tables.</p>

7334

7335

7336<p>

7337<strong>

7338 Heavy&mdash;</strong>

7339Concrete is incredibly heavy, making it a great option for windy areas but less than ideal if you plan to rearrange your outdoor furniture often.</p>

7340

7341

7342<p>

7343<strong>

7344 Absorbs Water&mdash;</strong>

7345You might be surprised to learn that concrete is prone to staining! Because the material is porous, concrete may absorb and stain if water and other spills are left uncleaned on its surface. For this reason, we recommend applying a sealer.</p>

7346

7347</div>

7348</div>

7349</div>

7350</div>

7351</div>

7352</div>

7353</div>

7354</div>

7355</div>

7356</div>

7357</div>

7358</div>

7359</div>
